Jamison Brereton

58 (354)
Ghee
V─Бmadeva Gautama
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 11
The Anukramaс╣З─л provides a bewildering variety of choices for the divinity of this hymn: Agni, or the Sun, or the waters, or the cowsтАФor ghee (ghr╠еta), the clarified melted butter regularly used as an oblation in sacrifice. The last is clearly correct.
Ghee is here given the same type of exalted, high-style rhetorical treatment as the other crucial ritual substance, soma, with which it is also identified in this poem. Phraseology appropriate to soma is applied to the streams of ghee throughout, and, like soma, ghee becomes the focus of mystical speculations and also the subject of vivid images. It is not surprising that this significant sacrificial substance should receive such poetic glorification, especially given the importance of cows and cow imagery in the R╠еgveda.
What should really surprise us is that only this poet in this late and final hymn in just one maс╣Зс╕Нala should have seen fit to make ghee his subject. Soma, after all, has a whole maс╣Зс╕Нala of 114 hymns to itself. Grammatical accident may help account for the difference: so╠Бma is grammatically masculine and thus easily personified, while ghr╠еta is grammatically neuter. However, the prominence of the cognate substance in Old Iranian (Aves. haoma, Old Persian hauma) and the existence of a lengthy praise hymn to deified Haoma in Younger Avestan (the H┼Нm Ya┼бt, Yasna 9тАУ10) testify to a long tradition of celebration of soma, which is not shared by ghee.644 IV.58

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sweet water swells up from the firmament; by the (solar) ray (man) obtains immortality; that which is he secret name of clarified butter is the tongue of the gods, the navel of ambrosia.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 17.89-99; the sweet water swells up from the firmament: samudr─Бd urmir madhum─Бn ud─Бrat: the meaning depends on the variants of meaning of samudra: samodante asmin yajam─Бnaс╕е, that in which worshippers delight, sacrificial fire; or, samudr─Бd dravanti ─Бpaс╕е, that from which waters rush, celestial fire, lightning;

┼кrmi = reward or consequence; second occurrence of ┼лrmi = rain; in the latter sence of ┼лrmi, samudra may mean antarkс╣гa, the firmament; samudra may also mean the udder of the cow, whence flows milk, samudravati, from which come ┼лrmi, ghi or butter; another interpretation restricts the objects to two: gh─л and agni, atra ann─Бdhy─Бsena ghс╣Ыtam st┼лyate pr─Бс╣З─Бdhy─Бsena ca agniс╕е; as a representative of food, gh─л is here praised, as that of vitality, agni; samudra is the ocean of gh─л, from which it rises as its wave, samudr─Бd ghс╣Ыta-mayad madhum─Бn rasav─Бn ┼лrmirudagacchat, and, having so risen, it pervades immortality by Agni, as the life of the world with whom it is combined: udgatya ca sa ┼лrmir-ansun─Б jagatpr─Бс╣Зabh┼лten─Бgnin─Б samaikibh┼лya amс╣Ыtatv─Бn vy─Бpnoti; in both interpretations, agni is intended, with whom gh─л, as the material of the oblation, is meant to be identified. That which is the secret name: ghс╣Ыtasya n─Бma guhyam yad asti jihv─Б dev─Бn─Бm amс╣Ыtasya n─Бbhiс╕е: i.e., the material of sacrifice commonly called gh─л is, in the mantras of the Veda, designated the tongue of the gods, being used metonymicaly for Agni; also the navel or binding, that is, the means of securing immortality for him who offers it in oblations. Since the ghс╣Ыta is intented to be the secret name, the reference intended may be to another principal oblation: the Soma

Jamison Brereton

From the sea a honeyed wave has arisen; along with the (soma-)plant it has reached all the way to immortality.
The name of Ghee that is hidden: тАЬthe tongue of the gods,тАЭ тАЬthe navel of the immortal.тАЭ

Griffith

FORTH from the ocean sprang the wave of sweetness: together with the stalk it turned to Amrta,
That which is holy oil’s mysterious title: but the Gods’ tongue is truly Amrta’s centre.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдереЛрджрдХрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рддреН) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рддреН (рдКрд░реНрдорд┐рдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╕рдореВрд╣рдГ (рдордзреБрдорд╛рдиреН) рдордзреБрд░рдЧреБрдгрдГ (рдЙрддреН) (рдЖрд░рддреН) рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрддрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ (рдЙрдк) (рдЕрдВрд╢реБрдирд╛) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпреЗрдг (рд╕рдореН) (рдЕрдореГрддрддреНрд╡рдореН) (рдЖрдирдЯреН) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ (рдШреГрддрд╕реНрдп) рдЙрджрдХрд╕реНрдп (рдирд╛рдо) (рдЧреБрд╣реНрдпрдореН) рдЧреБрдкреНрддрдореН (рдпрддреН) (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐) (рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛) (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдЕрдореГрддрд╕реНрдп) рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рддреНрдордХрд╕реНрдп рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╕реНрдп (рдирд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдирд╛рднрд┐рд░рд┐рд╡ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рднреВрдореЗрдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдкреЗрди рд╡рд╛рдпреБрджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдпрд╛рд╡рджреБрджрдХрдордиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рддрддреНрд░реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХреНрд░рдореЗрдг рдордзреБрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рдореГрддрд╛рддреНрдордХрдВ рднрд╡рддреАрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдд реерезрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рд╡рдпрдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдШреГрддрд╕реНрдп рдирд╛рдо рдкреНрд░ рдмреНрд░рд╡рд╛рдо рд╕реНрддреБрдордГ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдирдореЛрднрд┐рдГ рдирдорд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░реИрдГ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрднрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрд╛рдо рдЪ ред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реГрдвреЛ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рд╢рд╕реНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдорд╛рдирдорд┐рджрдореН рдЙрдк рд╢реГрдгрд╡рддреН рд╢реГрдгреБрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЪрддреБрдГрд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрдГ ред рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐ рд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдгрд┐ рд╡реЗрджрдЪрддреБрд╖реНрдЯрдпрд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдГ ред рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рдПрд╡рдореН ред рдЗрддрд░реЗрд╖реНрд╡рдкрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХреЛрдХреНрддрд╡реНрдпреБрддреНрдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпреЗрдпрдГ ред рдЧреМрд░рдГ рдЕрд░реБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдГ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢реЛ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рдПрддрддреН рдХрд░реНрдо рдЬрдЧрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╡рдореАрддреН рдЙрджреНрдЧрд┐рд░рддрд┐ рдирд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╣рддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe celebrate the name Ghс╣Ыta at this sacrifice, we offer it with adoration; may the four-horned Brahm─Б listen to its being glorified; the fair-complexioned-deity perfect this rite.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The four-horned brahm─Б: brahm─Б catuс╕е ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Еgaс╕е: brahm─Б, the mantra; parivс╣Ыс╕Нho devaс╕е, the augmented, developed, or great deity; his four horns are the four vedas; Brahm─Б is also explained as с╣Ъtij, priest; the fair-complexioned deity perfects this rite: avamid-gaura etat: gaura = yaj├▒a, with epithets catuс╕е ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Еga, the sacrifice with four priests, obtains the object for which it is solemnized; the verse is said to apply to Agni as the sun; but it is applied to gh─л. Since gh─л is the secret name for Soma, the object for which it is solemnized is Soma

Jamison Brereton

We will proclaim the name of Ghee; at this sacrifice here we will uphold it with reverences.
The formulator will hear it as it is being announced. The four-horned buffalo [=soma] has vomited it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The final p─Бda, with Soma (as a buffalo) vomiting (avam─лt) ghee, takes one aback, esp. after the high-style extolling that has preceded it. GeldnerтАЩs explanation, that тАЬgheeтАЭ is a secret sacred word (тАЬein sakrales GeheimwortтАЭ) and Soma reveals it, may be correct. But the bluntness of the verb still surprises, and I am inclined to think something further is going on. There are only two verb forms to тИЪvam in the RV, and the other one (v├бman X.108.8) also has speech as its object, but the evil Paс╣Зis as subj.

Note that the Paс╣Зis are found in vs. 4, as hiders of the ghee. Does our passage express some sort of rivalry between the two ritual substances? Or does it have to do with the Sautr─Бmaс╣Зi ritual, meant to cure Indra after vomiting?

Griffith

Let us declare aloud the name of Ghrta, and at this sacrifice hold it up with homage.
So let the Brahman hear the praise we utter. This hath the four-horned Buffalo emitted.

Geldner

Wir wollen den Namen des Ghrita verk├╝nden; bei diesem Opfer wollen wir ihn mit Ehrerbietung festhalten. Wenn er ausgesprochen wird, soll der Brahmanpriester darauf h├╢ren. Der vierh├╢rnige Gaurab├╝ffel hat ihn sich entschl├╝pfen lassen.

Grassmann

Wir wollen nun der Butter Wesen preisen, bei diesem Opfer demuthsvoU es hegen; Der Priester h├╢re das von uns gepries’ne; der B├╝ffel mit vier H├╢rnern spie hervor es.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFour are his horns; three are his feet; his heads are two, his hands are seven; the triple-bound showerer (of benefits) roars aloud; the mighty deity has entered among men.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This verse is preferentially applied to Agni, identified either with yaj├▒a or with ─Аditya; the four horns of the yaj├▒a are the four vedas; of ─Аditya, the four cardinal points of the horizon; the three feet of yaj├▒a are the three daily sacrifices; of ─Аditya, morning, noon, evening; the two heads of yaj├▒a are two particular ceremonies termed brahmaudanam and pravargya; of ─Аditya, day and night; the seven hands of yaj├▒a are the seven metres; of ─Аditya, the seven rays, or the six seasons and their aggregate, or the year, the seventh; the term vс╣Ыс╣гabha phal─Бn─Бm vaс╣Ыsit─Б, the rainer of rewards, applies to yaj├▒a and ─Аditya; so does roraite, he roars, implying the noise made by the repetition of the mantras of the vedas; the three bonds of yaj├▒a are: mantra, kalpa and br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the prayer, the ceremonial; the rationale of ─Аditya, the three regions, earth, mid-air and heaven; another view is to limit vс╣Ыс╣гabha k─Бm─Бnam varс╣гit─Б to yaj├▒a; the four horns are the priests: the hot─Б, udg─Бt─Б, adhvaryu and brahm─Б; the three feet are the three vedas; the two heads the havirdh─Бna and pravargya rites; the hands are the seven priests, or seven metres; the three bonds the three daily sacrifices; Nirukta 13.7 applies the verse to yaj├▒a

Jamison Brereton

Four are his horns, three his feet; two heads, seven hands are his. Triply bound, the bull keeps on roaring. The great god has entered mortals.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Clearly no bull found in nature. The numerology here presumably has to do with items in the ritual. For a conspectus of later interpr., see Witzel Got┼Н n.

Griffith

Four are his horns, three are the feet that bear him; his heads are two, his hands are seven in number.
Bound with a triple bond the Steer roars loudly: the mighty God hath entered in to mortals.

Geldner

Vier H├╢rner, drei F├╝├Яe hat er, zwei K├╢pfe, sieben H├дnde hat er. Dreifach gefesselt br├╝llt der Stier. Der gro├Яe Gott ist in die Sterblichen eingegangen.

Grassmann

Vier H├╢rner hat er, auf drei F├╝ssen steht er, zwei K├╢pfe sind ihm und der H├дnde sieben-, Dreifach gebunden br├╝llt der Stier gewaltig, der grosse Gott begab sich zu den Menschen.

  • рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдордГ
рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдм рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЬреЛ (рдорд╣рдГ) рдмреЬрд╛ рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдФрд░ рдЖрджрд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рджреЗрд╡рдГ) рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк рдФрд░ рд╕рдм рдХреЛ рд╕реБрдЦ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдиреН) рдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдорд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЖрджрд┐рдХреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЖ) рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ (рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрд╢) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рд╡реГрд╖рднрдГ) рдФрд░ рдЬреЛ рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рддреНрд░рд┐рдзрд╛) рддреАрди рд╢реНрд░рджреНрдзрд╛, рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрде рдФрд░ рдпреЛрдЧрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рд╕ рд╕реЗ (рдмрджреНрдзрдГ) рдмрдБрдзрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рд░реЛрд░рд╡реАрддрд┐) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рджреЗрддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЗрд╕ рдзрд░реНрдо рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдирд┐рддреНрдп рдФрд░ рдиреИрдорд┐рддреНрддрд┐рдХ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рдмреЛрдз рдХреЗ (рджреНрд╡реЗ) рджреЛ рдЙрдиреНрдирддрд┐ рдФрд░ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рд░реВрдк (рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖реЗ) рд╢рд┐рд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдкрдиреНрди (рддреНрд░рдпрдГ) рддреАрди рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдХрд░реНрдо, рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛ рдФрд░ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд░реВрдк (рдкрд╛рджрд╛рдГ) рдЪрд▓рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдкреИрд░ (рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐) рдФрд░ рдЪрд╛рд░ рд╡реЗрдж (рд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрд╛) рд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИрдВ рдФрд░ (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЗрд╕ рдзрд░реНрдо рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдХреЗ (рд╕рдкреНрдд) рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдп рд╡рд╛ рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рдХрд░реНрдореЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдп рдЕрдиреНрддрдГрдХрд░рдг рдФрд░ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рдпреЗ рд╕рд╛рдд (рд╣рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╕рдГ) рд╣рд╛рдереЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╣реИрдВ рдФрд░ рдЙрдХреНрдд рддреАрди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ рдмрдБрдзрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рднреА рдЬрд╛рдирдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЗрд╕ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рд╕реЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХреЗ рдЪрд╛рд░ рд╡реЗрдж рдФрд░ рдирд╛рдо, рдЖрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдд, рдЙрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЧ рдФрд░ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рдд рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡, рддреИрдЬрд╕, рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮ, рддреБрд░реАрдп рдФрд░ рдзрд░реНрдо, рдЕрд░реНрде, рдХрд╛рдо рдФрд░ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖ рдЖрджрд┐ рд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧ рд╣реИрдВред рддреАрди рд╕рд╡рди рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рддреНрд░реИрдХрд╛рд▓рд┐рдХ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдХрд░реНрдо рддреАрди рдХрд╛рд▓ рдХрд░реНрдо, рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛, рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдорди, рд╡рд╛рдгреА, рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдкрд╛рдж рд╣реИрдВред рджреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдФрд░ рдкрд░рдорд╛рд░реНрде рдирд┐рддреНрдп, рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдп рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк рдЙрджрдЧрдпрди рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрдгреАрдп рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдФрд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рд╢рд┐рд░ рд╣реИрдВред рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реА рдЖрджрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдд рдЫрдиреНрдж рд╕рд╛рдд рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддрд┐рдпрд╛рдБ, рд╕рд╛рдд рдкреНрд░рд╛рдг, рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рдХрд░реНрдореНрдореЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдп рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдФрд░ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдд рд╣рд╕реНрдд рд╣реИрдВред рддреАрди рдордиреНрддреНрд░, рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордг, рдХрд▓реНрдк рдФрд░ рд╣реГрджрдп, рдХрдгреНрда, рд╢рд┐рд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдг, рдордирди, рдирд┐рджрд┐рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдиреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпреНрдп, рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдХрд░реНрдо, рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдмреАрдЪ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдпрд╣ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдп рдФрд░ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдмреАрдЪ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рд╕рдм рдЬрд╛рдиреЗрдВ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпреЛ рдорд╣реЛ рджреЗрд╡реЛ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрд╢ рдпреЛ рд╡реГрд╖рднрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдзрд╛ рдмрджреНрдзреЛ рд░реЛрд░рд╡реАрддрд┐ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордиреЛ рдмреЛрдзрд╕реНрдп рджреНрд╡реЗ рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖реЗ рддреНрд░рдпрдГ рдкрд╛рджрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐ рд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрд╛ рдЪ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЪ рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╣рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╕рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдзрд╛ рдмрджреНрдзреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╢реНрдЪ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдГ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдереЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods discovered the Gh─л concealed by the Paс╣Зis, plural ced three-fold in the cow; Indra genitive rated one (portion), S┼лrya another, the (other gods) fabricated one from the resplendent (Agni), for the sake of the oblation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The paс╣Зis are asuras; the three forms or states in which the gh─л was deposited in the cow were milk, curds and butter, of which Indra engendered jaj─Бna, milk, S┼лrya butter, and the god (dev─Бsaс╕е) fabricated (tatakс╣гuс╕е) curds from the shining, ven─Бt, that is Agni; another rendering is dev─Бsaс╕е dvij─Бtayaс╕е, the twice-born

Jamison Brereton

Triply deposited, being hidden by the niggardsтАФthe gods discovered the ghee in the cow.
Indra begat one; the Sun begat one; from the seeker they fashioned one through their own power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was just noted, the Paс╣Зis (niggards) may be indirectly implicated in the verb avam─лt in 2d. Here they appear overtly, as the hiders of ghee – presumably a reference to their stealing of the cows, since the gods find the ghee in the cow in p─Бda b.

The threefold nature and creation of ghee has been variously interpreted; it again participates in the numerology of the hymn. I do not have a view on it.

Griffith

That oil in triple shape the Gods discovered laid down within the Cow, concealed by Panis.
Indra produced one shape, Surya another: by their own power they formed the third from Vena.

Geldner

Dreifach geteilt fanden das von den Pani┬┤s verborgene Ghrita die G├╢tter wieder in der Kuh. Indra hat das eine, Surya das eine erzeugt. Eines haben sie aus dem Seher durch eigene Kraft herausgebildet.

Grassmann

Die dreigetheilt versteckt war von den Pani’s, die Butter fanden in der Kuh die G├╢tter; Die eine zeugte Indra, Surja eine, und eine schufen selbst sie aus Verlangen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese hundred-channeled showers fall from the heart-delighting firmament, unobserved by the hostile (cloud); I look upon these showers of Gh─л, (and behold) the golden Vetasa in the midst of them.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Samudra, the showers is implied by the epithet ┼Ыata vraja, copious, either of water or gh─л;

Vetasa = Agni, either as lightning or the sun; or the fire of sacrifice; another interpretation: et─Б arс╣гanti, v─Бc─Б udgacchanti, these words originate from the ocean of the water of faith, purified by the metres and other supplementary portions of the Vedas, amidst which words the с╣Ыс╣гis see the golden form of Agni, for Agni is the deity presiding over speech, or holy texts, agnir hi vac─Бm adhiс╣гс╣нh─Бtri devat─Б

Jamison Brereton

These (streams) rush from the sea found in the heart. Having a hundred barriers, they are not to be spotted by the cheat,
but I keep gazing upon the streams of ghee. A golden reed is in their midst.

Jamison Brereton Notes

тАЬMyтАЭ ability to see the ghee streams indirectly attests to my good character, since the cheat cannot see them.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey flow uninterruptedly like plural asing rivers, purified by the mind that is seated in the heart; these streams of Gh─л descend (upon the fire), like deer flying from the hunter.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The allusion is to the gh─л poured from the ladle on the fire; antahс╣Ыd─Б manas─Б: hс╣Ыdayamadhya gatena cittena, by the mind gone within the heart;

┼Ъ┼лghan─Бsaс╕е: ─Б┼Ыu gantryaс╕е (Nirukta 6.1)

Jamison Brereton

These nourishing liquids flow together like streams, being purified within by heart and mind.
These waves of ghee rush, like wild beasts retreating from a javelin.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c combines et─Б╠Бarс╣гanti from 5a with a variant of the repeated ghr╠еt├бsya dh─Б╠Бr─Бс╕е, namely ┼лrm├бyo ghrt├бsya ╠е .

Each of these 6 vss. contains the phrase ghrt├бsya dh ╠е ─Б╠Бr─Бс╕е (or equiv.: ┼лrm├бyo ghrt├бsya ╠е in 6c).

Griffith

Like rivers our libations flow together, cleansing themselves in inmost heart and spirit.
The streams of holy oil pour swiftly downward like the wild beasts that fly before the bowman.

рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреЛрдГ рд╕реНрдпрдиреНрджрдорд╛рдирд╛рдпрд╛ рдирджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рдЗрд╡ рдЙрджрдХрд╛рдиреАрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдзреНрд╡рдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╡рдгрд╡рддрд┐ рджреЗрд╢реЗ рд╢реВрдШрдирд╛рд╕рдГ рдЖрд╢реБрдЧрдиреНрддреНрд░реНрдпрдГ ред тАШ рдЖрд╢реБ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪ рд╢реБ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдирд╛рдордиреА рднрд╡рддрдГ ’ ( рдирд┐рд░реБ. рем. рез ) рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрддрдореН ред рд╡рд╛рддрдкреНрд░рдорд┐рдпрдГ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд╡рддреН рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╡реЗрдЧрд╛рдГ рдпрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдорд╣рддреНрдпрдГ рдШреГрддрд╕реНрдп рдзрд╛рд░рд╛рдГ рдкрддрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреНрдпрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реБрдкрд░рд┐ ред рдШреГрддрдореБрджрдХрдорд┐рддрд┐ рдкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреЛрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрддреНрдпрддреНрд░ рдЗрд╡рд╢рдмреНрджреЛрд╜рдирд░реНрдердХрдГ ред рд╕реНрдпрдиреНрджрдирд╕рд╛рдзрдирд╛рджрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рджреБрдХреНрддрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛ рдШреГрддрдзрд╛рд░рд╛ рдЙрджрдХрдзрд╛рд░рд╛рдГ рдкрддрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рднреВрдореМ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдШреГрддрд╕рдВрд╕реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдпрдГ рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ рдорд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд╛рднреВрддрд╛рдиреН рдкрд░рд┐рдзреАрдиреН рднрд┐рдиреНрджрдиреН рдКрд░реНрдорд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд░рд╕реИрдГ рдкрд┐рдиреНрд╡рдорд╛рдирдГ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдорд╛рдиреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдЙрджрдХрдорд┐рддрд┐ рдкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╛ рджрд┐рд╢реЛ рднрд┐рдиреНрджрдиреНрдиреВрд░реНрдорд┐рднрд┐рдГ рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧреИрдГ рдкрд┐рдиреНрд╡рдорд╛рдиреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдЕрд░реБрд╖реЛ рди рд╡рд╛рдЬреА рдЖрд░реЛрдЪрдорд╛рдиреЛ рдЧрд░реНрд╡реЗрдг рдЧрдордирд╢реАрд▓реЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡ рдЗрд╡ ред рд╕ рдпрдерд╛ рднрд┐рдиреНрджрдиреН рдкрд┐рдиреНрд╡рдорд╛рдирд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe stream of Gh─л fall copious, swift as the wind, and rapid as the waters of a river down a declivity, breaking through the confining banks, and hurrying on with their waves, like a high-spirited steed.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Swift as the wind: v─Бta pramiyaс╕е vay┼лvat prakс╣Ыс╣гс╣нavega; the comparison may be to Sindhu, a river agitated by the wind; breaking through the confining banks: k─Бс╣гс╣нh─Б bhindan urmibhiс╕е pinvam─Бnaс╕е: k─Бс╣гс╣нh─Б = limiting circles; mary─Бd─Бbh┼лt─Бn paridh─лn limits within which the flowing butter increases with its juice; ghс╣Ыta may also mean water, when sindhu will imploy antarikс╣гa

Jamison Brereton

As if on the straightaway of a river, they flyтАФthe youthfully exuberant ones, swift-battering, confounding the windтАФ
the streams of gheeтАФlike a ruddy prizewinning horse splitting
the wooden race-course barriers [/splintering the sticks (in their current)], swelling with their waves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A difficult verse, primarily because of the two hapaxes, ┼Ы┼лghan─Б╠Бsaс╕е and v─Б╠Бtapramiyaс╕е. The former is taken by Geldner as тАШwhirlpools, eddiesтАЩ (Wirbel)(followed not terribly enthusiastically by Renou) on no particular basis, and others have added their own at best weakly supported tr.: e.g., Thieme тАШcow-killingтАЩ [┼Ы┼л- тЖР *p┼Ыu-] KlSch. 52), most recently Witzel Got┼Н тАШdie schwellenden MassenтАЩ (presumably with root noun 1st member and later ghana- тАШclump, massтАЩ). The interpr. reflected in the published translation is no stronger than these others. It begins with ghan├б- тАШsmiterтАЩ (well represented in the RV), as ThiemeтАЩs also must. But for 1st member I assume a zero-grade of ─Б┼Ы├║- тАШswiftтАЩ (for the uncertainties of the initial of the PIE тАШswiftтАЩ words, see EWA s.v.) with lengthening at compound seam. With two such ad hoc assumptions, this interpr. is simply a place-holder.

As for v─Б╠Бtapramiyaс╕е, there is no question about its component parts, merely about how they fit together. -pramiyaс╕е patterns with the nearby forms IV.54.4 pram├нye (тАШto be violatedтАЩ) and IV.55.7 pram├нyam (тАШto violateтАЩ). It also strongly recalls I.24.6 n├б y├й v─Б╠Бtasya pramin├бnti ├бbhvam тАЬnor those [=the gods] who confound the windтАЩs formless mass.тАЭ As Oldenberg points out, this latter passage fixes the interpr. of our cmpd.: the first member must be functionally the object of the 2nd. The problem is the accent; it should be a bahuvr─лhi, not a tatpuruс╣гa. See, however, Scarlatta (388), who suggests a plausible bahuvr─лhi interpr. тАШdie Schm├дlerung des Windes habendтАЩ, with the first member essentially an objective genitive. The point is that the speed and violence of the streams are stronger than those of the wind, which is thus confounded.

I read k─Б╠Бс╣гс╣нh─Б(с╕е) in both simile and frame: in the simile it refers to the wooden barriers of the race-course that the horse splits in his speeding around the course, in the frame to sticks floating in the current of the streams and split (against rocks vel sim.) by the violent speed of that current. (Of course the тАЬframeтАЭ here is itself metaphorical, since these are streams of ghee, not actual watercourses.)

As rushing down the rapids of a river, flow swifter than the wind the vigorous currents,
The streams of oil in swelling fluctuation like a red courser bursting through the fences.

The streams of holy oil attain the fuel, and Jatavedas joyfully receives them.

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ ! рдкрд┐рдиреНрд╡рдорд╛рдиреЛрд╜рд╣рдВ рдпрдерд╛ рд╢реВрдШрдирд╛рд╕реЛ рдпрд╣реНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╛рддрдкреНрд░рдорд┐рдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдзреНрд╡рдиреЗ рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреЛрд░рд┐рд╡ рдкрддрдпрдиреНрддреНрдпрд░реБрд╖реЛ рд╡рд╛рдЬреА рди рдШреГрддрд╕реНрдп рдзрд╛рд░рд╛ рдКрд░реНрдореНрдорд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдард╛ рднрд┐рдиреНрджрдБрд╕реНрддрдереЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рднрд┐рдирджреНрдорд┐ рееренрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe streams of Gh─л incline to Agni as devoted wives, auspicious and smiling, to a husband; they feed (the flame) like fuel, and J─Бtavedas, propitiated, accepts them.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They floatтАФlike lovely young women to (marriage) assembliesтАФ smiling, to Agni.
The streams of ghee approach the kindling sticks. (Agni) J─Бtavedas delights, taking pleasure in them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The violence of the movement of the ghee-streams in the preceding vs. is abruptly replaced by the placid and benign approach of these same streams in this vs. _________ 11
Renou points out the ring composition of 11d m├бdhumantaс╣Г ta ┼лrm├нm and 1a ┼лrm├нr m├бdhum─Бn.

English translation:

тАЬI contemplate these streams of Gh─л as they flow from where the Soma is effused, where the sacrifice (is solemnized), as maidens decorating themselves with unguents to go to the bridegroom.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I keep gazing upon them, who are like maidens smearing on unguent to go to their wedding.
Where the soma is pressed, where the sacrifice (is performed), toward that do the streams of ghee go purifying themselves. с│У

As maidens dock themselves with gay adornment to join the bridal feast, I now behold them.
Where Soma flows and sacrifice is ready, thither the streams of holy oil are running.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Priests) address the pious praise, (the source) of herds of cattle; bestow upon us auspicious riches; convey this our sacrifice to the gods, (where at) the streams of Gh─л with sweetness descend.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Priests: the text has no nominative native; с╣Ъtvijaс╕е, priests are impied; an alternative implied term may be dev─Бс╕е, gods; the pious praise the source of herds of cattle: suс╣гс╣нutim gavyam ─Бjim: ─Бjim = gosambandhin─Бm saс╣Еgh─Бtam, the number or collections related to cattle; or, it may mean the abundance of water; another interpretation: agni = yaj├▒a (sacrifice);

Gavya = gh─л; gods, approach the pious praise, and, the sacrifice at which gh─л is offered

Jamison Brereton

Rush toward the lovely praise hymn, to the contest for cows; on us confer auspicious chattels.
Lead this sacrifice here to the divinities for us. The streams of ghee purify themselves like honey. с│У

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe whole world, (Agni), finds an asylum in your effulgence, whether it be in the ocean, in the heart (of man), in the life (of living beings), in the assemblage of the waters, or in warfare; may we attain the sweet-flavoured wave which is established in your (essence).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dh─Бman te vi┼Ыvam bhuvanam adhi┼Ыritam: dh─Бman = tejaс╕е sth─Бne, in the plural ce of brightness or heat (or vibhutyam, superhuman power); the purport is to identify all things with Agni, present in the ocean as submarine fire, in men as vai┼Ыv─Бnara, an etymological pun from vi┼Ыva, all and nara, man; in life, ─Бyuс╣гi, as the vital principle, or ─Бyus. may mean food, anna, when the digestive fire is intended; in the assembled waters or the firmament, as lightning; in war, as the metaphorical fire of valour; that sweet-flavoured wave: ┼лrmiс╕е ya ─Бbhс╣Ыtaс╕е, the wave which is so deposited, sth─Бpitaс╕е, may imply either the butter of the oblation, or water in the shape of rain. The reference to madhu in this and previous verse, establish that the implied reference is o Soma

All the living world is firmly fixed in your domain, within the sea in your heart, within your lifespan.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рднрдЧрд╡рдиреН ! рдпрд╕реНрдп рддреЗ рдзрд╛рдордиреНрдирдиреНрддрдГ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реЗ рд╣реГрджреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдпреБрд╖реНрдпрдкрд╛рдордиреАрдХреЗ рд╕рдорд┐рдереЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рднреБрд╡рдирдордзрд┐ рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдпрд╕реНрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рд░рд╛рднреГрддрд╕реНрддрдВ рдордзреБрдордиреНрддрдореВрд░реНрдорд┐рдорд╛рдирдиреНрджрдВ рд╡рдпрдорд╢реНрдпрд╛рдо рддрджреБрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рддрддрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдо реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдзрд╛рдордиреН) рдЖрдзрд╛рд░реЗ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдореН (рднреБрд╡рдирдореН) рдЬрдЧрддреН (рдЕрдзрд┐) рдЙрдкрд░рд┐ (рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдореН) рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдореН (рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ) (рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реЗ) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ (рд╣реГрджрд┐) рд╣реГрджрдпреЗ (рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ) рдордзреНрдпреЗ (рдЖрдпреБрд╖рд┐) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЗ (рдЕрдкрд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдирд╛рдореН (рдЕрднреАрдХреЗ) рд╕реИрдиреНрдпреЗ (рд╕рдорд┐рдереЗ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рдпрдГ) (рдЖрднреГрддрдГ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рджреН рдзреГрддрдГ (рддрдореН) (рдЕрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдо) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдо (рдордзреБрдордиреНрддрдореН) рдорд╛рдзреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдЧреБрдгреЛрдкреЗрддрдореН (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдКрд░реНрдорд┐рдореН) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдореН реерезрезрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ! рдЬреЛ рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдЬрдЧрд╛рдд рдЕрднрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдКрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░реВрди рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░реВрди рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрдпрд╛рдпреА рд░реВрдкрд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд рдЖрд╣реЗ рд╡ рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдХреГрдкреЗрдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди, рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдпреБреБрд╖реНрдп рд╡ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдп рдорд┐рд│рддреЛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреАрдЪ рдирд┐рд░рдВрддрд░ рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░рд╛. рее резрез рее
